Proof from the Interconnectedness of Diverse Creatures
Maturidi argues from the interconnectedness of diverse creatures for a single manager.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the interconnectedness of all creation, despite its diversity, points to a single Creator.

Core Idea
Diverse creation, unified system — one Manager required.

Maturidi presents a second proof for tawhid, drawing attention to how everything in creation is interconnected. Even though the heavens are vastly different from the earth, and regions are far apart, they all serve each other. This intricate web of mutual benefit cannot be the work of multiple administrators, but must be the design of one wise Manager.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how Maturidi builds his argument step by step.
2
Identify the key observations
List the observations Maturidi makes about creation: differences between heaven and earth, distances, provisions, and how they are interconnected through benefits.
Pay attention to the phrase 'جعلت متصلة بالمنافع'.
3
Understand the logical deduction
Maturidi argues that if there were multiple managers, the sources of these benefits could not converge. Understand why this impossibility leads to the conclusion of one Manager.
4
Reflect on the Quranic verse and six directions
Read the Quranic verse quoted and the comment about bodies having six directions. Consider how uniformity in dimensionality supports oneness.
5
Appreciate the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that one Manager gathered all under one meaning. Reflect on the coherence of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني أن الأجناس على اختلافها وتباعد ما بينها من نحو السماء والأرض، وأطراف الأرض، وبعد أرزاق أهلها جعلت متصلة بالمنافع، حتى كان كل أنواع الخارج من الأرض يكون بأسباب السماء و حاجات كل أهل البلدان منتشرة في جميع الأطراف، ومعاش البشر مجعول في أنواع المكاسب؛ على هذا دار أمر الجميع. فلو كان ذلك لعدد، لم يحتمل أن ترجع منابعها إلى من له العالم من الخلق، على اختلاف العالم؛ ثبت أن مدبر ذلك كله واحد. وعلى ما ذكرت الأوقات من الليل والنهار والساعات، ودخول بعض في بعض على قدر الحاجات، وهذا - والله أعلم - معنى قوله : ما ترى في خلق الرحمن من تفاوت [الملك، ٣/٦٧]. فهذا، ما جعلت الأجسام، وهي الأعيان على جهات ست. ثبت أن مدبر كل على اختلاف الأجناس واحد، حتى جمع الكل تحت معنى واحد. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And the second: that the kinds [of creatures] despite their differences and the vast distances between them, such as the heaven and earth, the extremities of the earth, the remoteness of the provisions of its inhabitants, are made interconnected with benefits, such that every type of what comes out of the earth is caused by the causes of the heaven, and the needs of every people of the lands are spread throughout all regions, and the livelihood of mankind is placed in various types of earnings; upon this the whole affair runs. So if that were due to a number [of gods], it would not be possible for their sources to return to the one who has the world from the creation, given the diversity of the world; it is established that the manager of all that is one. And according to what has been mentioned of times: night and day and hours, and the entry of some into others according to the measure of needs, and this — God knows best — is the meaning of His saying: 'You do not see in the creation of the Most Merciful any discrepancy' [al-Mulk 67:3]. So this is that the bodies, which are the essences, are upon six directions. It is established that the manager of everything despite the difference of kinds is one, until He gathered all under one meaning. And there is no power except with God.

Commentary
This passage presents a second argument from creation, focusing on the interconnectedness of all things. Maturidi points out that despite the immense diversity of creation — the heavens and earth, different regions, and varied provisions — everything is interconnected. The needs of all people are served through a unified system where the earth's produce depends on heavenly causes (like rain), and livelihoods come from various sources. If there were multiple administrators, it would be impossible for all these to converge on a single source. He then brings in the consistency of time (night and day) and quotes the Quranic verse about no discrepancy in creation. The reference to bodies having six directions (up, down, front, back, right, left) underscores the uniform dimensionality of all physical things, further supporting a single Creator. The proof culminates in the assertion that one Manager has brought everything under one meaning (i.e., one purpose and order).

Proof from the Dual Nature of Substances
Maturidi proves tawhid from the dual nature of substances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's proof for the oneness of God based on the dual nature of substances.

Core Idea
No substance is purely beneficial or harmful—this shows one Manager.

Maturidi presents a third proof for tawhid from the nature of created substances. He observes that nothing in creation is exclusively good or bad; the same thing can be beneficial in one context and harmful in another. This points to a single wise Manager who combines opposites. In this lesson, we will examine this argument.

Guided Path

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثالث أنه لا يُوجد جوهر واحد يرجع بجوهره إلى معنى واحد من الضرر أو النفع، أو الخبث أو الطيب، أو النعمة أو البلاء، بل كل شيء يوصف بالخبث فهو يصير طيبا في وجه ولغير من له خبث، وكذلك سائر الصفات. وعلى ذلك أحوال الأشياء: إنها ليست على نفع بكل حال أو ضرر بكل حال. ثبت أن مدير ذلك كله واحد، حتى جمع في كل وجوه المضار والمنافع، ولم يجعل شيئا ذا نوع ليُعلم أنه عن أصل يرجع إلى جوهره، أو عن تدبير عدد يفعل كل جهة فيتناقض بما تفرد كل بالجهة التي هي منه. ولا قوة إلا بالله.

Commentary
This passage presents a third proof from the nature of created substances. Maturidi observes that no substance is inherently and exclusively beneficial or harmful; the same thing can be beneficial in one context and harmful in another. This indicates that there is a wise Manager who combines opposites in a coherent way. If there were multiple gods, each would have a specific direction, leading to contradiction. But the fact that everything serves multiple purposes and that there is a balance shows that a single Creator is responsible. The argument refutes the possibility of multiple deities by showing the unity of design behind the complexity of creation.

Proof from the Harmony of Opposing Natures
Maturidi argues from the coexistence of opposing natures in bodies for a single administrator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the coexistence of opposing natures in bodies to argue for a single divine administrator.

Core Idea
Opposing natures held together point to a single Manager.

How can fire and water coexist within the same body without destroying it? Maturidi sees this as a clear sign of a wise Administrator holding them together. In this lesson, we examine his argument that the unity of natural forces implies a single divine manager.

This is a classic kalam argument for tawhid.

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the harmony of opposing elements in bodies. Yet they coexist in a stable manner, which indicates a single Administrator who holds them together with gentleness and wisdom. If there were multiple gods, the natural opposition would manifest itself, causing corruption. The argument is incomplete at the end of the page, but the reasoning is clear: the unity of natural forces points to a single divine manager.

The First Proof from Time and Resources
Maturidi's first proof from the order of times and provisions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's first argument that the ordered distribution of resources and the measured alternation of night and day point to a single Provider and Manager.

Core Idea
The harmony of times and sustenance disproves multiple gods.

In this passage, Maturidi begins a series of arguments demonstrating that the observable order in the universe cannot be the product of several deities. He first draws attention to how human needs and livelihoods are distributed across the earth, and how days and nights interlock with precision. The Quranic verse 'You see not in the creation of the Most Merciful any disparity' (67:3) encapsulates this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Maturidi builds the argument.
2
Identify the key observations
Look for the observations: needs spread in all regions, livelihoods in various types, and the interlocking of night and day according to need.
3
Understand the Quranic reference
Maturidi cites Quran 67:3. Reflect on how this verse supports his reasoning.
4
Connect to the conclusion
See how the observation leads to the conclusion that the manager (mudabbir) of all this must be one.
The phrase 'for a number' means multiple gods.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع يكون بأسباب السماء و حاجات كل أهل البلدان منتشرة في جميع الأطراف، ومعاش البشر مجعول في أنواع المكاسب؛ على هذا دار أمر الجميع. فلو كان ذلك لعدد ، لم يحتمل أن ترجع منابعها إلى من له العالم من الخلق ، على اختلاف العالم؛ ثبت أن مدبر ذلك كله واحد. وعلى ما ذكرت الأوقات من الليل والنهار والساعات، ودخول بعض في بعض على قدر الحاجات، وهذا ـ والله أعلم - معنى قوله : ما ترى في خلق الرحمن من تفاوت [الملك، ٣/٦٧]. فهذا، ما جعلت الأجسام، وهي الأعيان على جهات ست. ثبت أن مدبر كل على اختلاف الأجناس واحد، حتى جمع الكل تحت معنى واحد. ولا قوة إلا بالله. والثالث أنه لا يُوجد جوهر واحد يرجع بجوهره إلى معنى واحد من الضرر أو النفع، أو الخبث أو الطيب، أو النعمة أو البلاء، بل كل شيء يوصف بالخبث فهو يصير طيبا في وجه ولغير من له خبث، وكذلك سائر الصفات. وعلى ذلك أحوال الأشياء: إنها ليست على نفع بكل حال أو ضرر بكل حال. ثبت أن مدير ذلك كله واحد، حتى جمع في كل وجوه المضار والمنافع، ولم يجعل شيئا ذا نوع ليُعلم أنه عن أصل يرجع إلى جوهره، أو عن تدبير عدد يفعل كل جهة فيتناقض بما تفرد كل بالجهة التي هي منه . ولا قوة إلا بالله . وأيضا إن الأعيان تراها تحت حد الأجسام كلها، وهي مجتمعة على طبائع متضادة، حقها التنافر والتباعد بما بينها من التعادى الذي لو توهم تركها وطباعها لكان في ذلك فساد الكل. فثبت أن مدبر الجميع بينها واحد ؛ يجمعهم باللطف، ويحبس ضرر كل عن غيره بالحكمة العجيبة التي لا تبلغها الأوهام. ولو كان لعددٍ لجرى فيها حق الاختلاف والتضاد، على ما عليه إرادة الفاعلين من السد بغيرهم وبصنع غيرهم ليتبين صنعه. وبالله النجاة. وأمكن الجمع بين الحرفين في جميع ما ينتهي إليه الاعتبار من الإشارة إلى الدلالة أنها تخرج على النظر إلى الأحوال والأفعال. فالأحوال هي أن يكونوا في جميع معاني الربوبية سواء، فيكون في ذلك تدافع وتمانع مع ما كان ذلك صفة فردٍ سموه عددًا، أو تختلف ، فيكون الأتمّ لها أحق بالربوبية. وأما الأفعال فما ذكرتُ من اتساق جميع العالم مع تناقض الطبائع وتضادها صارت كأنها أشكال في قوام بعض ببعض، وكون بعض لبعض عونا و ناصرا في البقاء. وإن كانوا بالوجه الذي ذكرت ثبت أن ذلك التألف مع التضاد لا يُحتمل إلا بمدبر حكيم عليم لطيف، لا ينازع في التدبير، ولا يُخالف في التقدير ولا قوة إلا بالله .
With the causes of the sky and the needs of all the people of the lands being spread in all regions, and the livelihood of humanity made in various types of earnings; upon this the whole matter revolves. So if that were due to a number [of gods], it would not be possible for their sources to return to the one who [alone] has the world from among the creation, despite the diversity of the world; it is established that the manager of all that is one. And according to what is mentioned of the times of night and day and the hours, and the interpenetration of one into another according to needs, and this — and God knows best — is the meaning of His saying: ‘You see not in the creation of the Most Merciful any disparity’ [Q. 67:3]. So this, that bodies — which are the entities — were made on six directions. It is established that the manager of everything despite the diversity of kinds is one, until He gathered the whole under one meaning. And there is no power except through God. And the third: that there is not found a single atom that returns in its essence to one meaning of harm or benefit, or bad or good, or blessing or trial; rather, everything described as bad becomes good in some aspect and for other than the one who has badness, and likewise the rest of the attributes. Upon that are the states of things: they are not [entirely] beneficial in every case or harmful in every case. It is established that the director of all that is one, until He gathered in all aspects of harms and benefits, and did not make anything of a kind so that it be known whether it is from an origin returning to its essence, or from the management of a number each doing a direction, thus conflicting with each being unique in the direction that is from it. And there is no power except through God. Also, the entities are seen under the limit of all bodies, and they are combined upon opposing natures, while their right is to repel and separate due to the enmity between them, such that if one imagined leaving them to their natures, the corruption of the whole would result. So it is established that the manager of all between them is one; He brings them together with gentleness, and restrains the harm of each from the other with amazing wisdom that imaginations cannot reach. And if it were due to a number, the truth of disagreement and opposition would run in them, according to what the will of the agents [requires] from repelling others and from the making of others so that His making becomes clear. And with God is deliverance. And it is possible to combine the two aspects in all that the consideration ends at from the indication that it emerges upon looking at the states and acts. The states: that they be equal in all meanings of lordship, so in that there would be repulsion and prevention, since that was the description of an individual they call number, or they differ, so the most perfect of them would be more entitled to lordship. As for the acts: what I mentioned of the harmony of the entire world despite the contradiction of natures and their opposition, they become as if they are forms in the subsistence of some by some, and some being for some a help and supporter in survival. And if they were in the way I mentioned, it is established that that harmony with opposition is not possible except through a wise, knowing, gentle Manager, who is not disputed in management, nor opposed in determination, and there is no power except through God.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part proof of divine unity (tawḥīd) from the observable order and coherence of the world. Maturidi presents several arguments, each building on the harmony of creation despite diversity and opposition.

First argument: The distribution of needs and livelihoods across all regions, and the interlocking times (day and night, seasons) that follow a measured pattern, point to a single provider and manager. If there were multiple gods, it would be impossible for the resources to originate from one source without conflict. Maturidi cites Quran 67:3 as evidence that there is no disparity in creation.

Second argument (introduced by 'فهذا'): Bodies are created on six directions (dimensions) and yet are unified under one meaning, necessitating a single manager.

Third argument: No atom is purely harmful or beneficial, good or bad; things change in different contexts. This mixture of qualities across all things shows that no object is fixed in its nature, which would be expected if it came from a single essence or from multiple directorial forces each imposing a fixed character. The fact that everything has varying opposites indicates a single director who balances all aspects.

Fourth argument: Entities exist under the category of bodies and possess opposing natures; their natural tendency is conflict and dissolution. Yet we see them coexisting and supporting each other. This survival cannot happen without a single wise manager who restrains harm and preserves order. If there were multiple gods, their natural opposition would lead to chaos.

Fifth argument: Considering the states (aḥwāl) and acts (afʿāl) of gods if there were multiple: either they are equal in lordship, leading to mutual opposition, or one is superior, and the superior alone deserves lordship. The actual harmony of the world, with its many opposing forces working together, cannot be the result of multiple agents but only of a single, wise, all-knowing, and gentle manager who has no rival in determination.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbir)
تفاوت (tafāwut)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The order in the world could be maintained by multiple gods cooperating.
Correction: Maturidi argues that multiple sources would necessarily lead to conflict or inconsistency; cooperation among independent gods is impossible without a higher authority.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi use to support his first argument?
A) Quran 67:3
B) Quran 112:1
C) The six directions
D) The idea of atoms

Key Takeaway
The orderly distribution of resources and the precise cycle of day and night point to a single Manager, not many.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the consistent alternation of night and day, the rain that falls, and the food you eat, does your heart naturally turn in gratitude to the single Manager who orchestrates it all—or do you take these patterns for granted and live as if your provisions are in your own control? What one habit can you adopt today to consciously connect every provision to its true Source?
?
The proof shows that if multiple gods existed, the sources of provision would not return to one. In your life, are there areas where you seek security from multiple sources—wealth, status, relationships—as if they are independent of Allah? How can you reorient your trust so that you rely solely on the One who manages all things?
?
Allah says, 'You see not in the creation of the Most Merciful any disparity.' When you witness apparent chaos or injustice in the world, do you doubt the unity and perfection of the Manager, or do you trust that the overall design is flawless? What would it take for you to see beyond the surface and affirm that there is no flaw in His creation?

The Unity from Bodies and Mixed Qualities
Maturidi's arguments from the uniformity of bodies and the mixture of qualities in atoms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's two arguments: that all bodies are unified under one meaning despite different directions, and that no atom is purely fixed in harm or benefit, both showing a single director.

Core Idea
Bodies and atoms show that no single fixed nature exists; all quality mixtures point to one Director.

Maturidi continues his proofs by drawing attention to bodies and atoms. He observes that all bodies are created on six directions, yet they are unified under one meaning. Then he notes that no single atom is entirely harmful or beneficial, good or bad, blessing or trial; rather, everything can change its character in different contexts. This variability indicates that things are not driven by their own fixed essences but by a single wise director who balances all outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that there are two separate arguments here.
2
Analyze the first argument about bodies
Maturidi says bodies are made on six directions, yet the manager is one who gathered all under one meaning. How does this prove unity?
The six directions refer to spatial dimensions; despite diversity of bodies, they all share the same structure of dimensions.
3
Analyze the second argument about atoms
The third argument: no atom is purely harmful or beneficial. Why does this imply a single director?
If atoms were purely one attribute, they could be attributed to different gods. But the mixture suggests a single source that combines opposites.
4
Synthesize
Combine both arguments: the unity in diversity of bodies and the mixture of qualities across all things both point to a single manager, not many.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع يكون بأسباب السماء و حاجات كل أهل البلدان منتشرة في جميع الأطراف، ومعاش البشر مجعول في أنواع المكاسب؛ على هذا دار أمر الجميع. فلو كان ذلك لعدد ، لم يحتمل أن ترجع منابعها إلى من له العالم من الخلق ، على اختلاف العالم؛ ثبت أن مدبر ذلك كله واحد. وعلى ما ذكرت الأوقات من الليل والنهار والساعات، ودخول بعض في بعض على قدر الحاجات، وهذا ـ والله أعلم - معنى قوله : ما ترى في خلق الرحمن من تفاوت [الملك، ٣/٦٧]. فهذا، ما جعلت الأجسام، وهي الأعيان على جهات ست. ثبت أن مدبر كل على اختلاف الأجناس واحد، حتى جمع الكل تحت معنى واحد. ولا قوة إلا بالله. والثالث أنه لا يُوجد جوهر واحد يرجع بجوهره إلى معنى واحد من الضرر أو النفع، أو الخبث أو الطيب، أو النعمة أو البلاء، بل كل شيء يوصف بالخبث فهو يصير طيبا في وجه ولغير من له خبث، وكذلك سائر الصفات. وعلى ذلك أحوال الأشياء: إنها ليست على نفع بكل حال أو ضرر بكل حال. ثبت أن مدير ذلك كله واحد، حتى جمع في كل وجوه المضار والمنافع، ولم يجعل شيئا ذا نوع ليُعلم أنه عن أصل يرجع إلى جوهره، أو عن تدبير عدد يفعل كل جهة فيتناقض بما تفرد كل بالجهة التي هي منه . ولا قوة إلا بالله . وأيضا إن الأعيان تراها تحت حد الأجسام كلها، وهي مجتمعة على طبائع متضادة، حقها التنافر والتباعد بما بينها من التعادى الذي لو توهم تركها وطباعها لكان في ذلك فساد الكل. فثبت أن مدبر الجميع بينها واحد ؛ يجمعهم باللطف، ويحبس ضرر كل عن غيره بالحكمة العجيبة التي لا تبلغها الأوهام. ولو كان لعددٍ لجرى فيها حق الاختلاف والتضاد، على ما عليه إرادة الفاعلين من السد بغيرهم وبصنع غيرهم ليتبين صنعه. وبالله النجاة. وأمكن الجمع بين الحرفين في جميع ما ينتهي إليه الاعتبار من الإشارة إلى الدلالة أنها تخرج على النظر إلى الأحوال والأفعال. فالأحوال هي أن يكونوا في جميع معاني الربوبية سواء، فيكون في ذلك تدافع وتمانع مع ما كان ذلك صفة فردٍ سموه عددًا، أو تختلف ، فيكون الأتمّ لها أحق بالربوبية. وأما الأفعال فما ذكرتُ من اتساق جميع العالم مع تناقض الطبائع وتضادها صارت كأنها أشكال في قوام بعض ببعض، وكون بعض لبعض عونا و ناصرا في البقاء. وإن كانوا بالوجه الذي ذكرت ثبت أن ذلك التألف مع التضاد لا يُحتمل إلا بمدبر حكيم عليم لطيف، لا ينازع في التدبير، ولا يُخالف في التقدير ولا قوة إلا بالله .
With the causes of the sky and the needs of all the people of the lands being spread in all regions, and the livelihood of humanity made in various types of earnings; upon this the whole matter revolves. So if that were due to a number [of gods], it would not be possible for their sources to return to the one who [alone] has the world from among the creation, despite the diversity of the world; it is established that the manager of all that is one. And according to what is mentioned of the times of night and day and the hours, and the interpenetration of one into another according to needs, and this — and God knows best — is the meaning of His saying: ‘You see not in the creation of the Most Merciful any disparity’ [Q. 67:3]. So this, that bodies — which are the entities — were made on six directions. It is established that the manager of everything despite the diversity of kinds is one, until He gathered the whole under one meaning. And there is no power except through God. And the third: that there is not found a single atom that returns in its essence to one meaning of harm or benefit, or bad or good, or blessing or trial; rather, everything described as bad becomes good in some aspect and for other than the one who has badness, and likewise the rest of the attributes. Upon that are the states of things: they are not [entirely] beneficial in every case or harmful in every case. It is established that the director of all that is one, until He gathered in all aspects of harms and benefits, and did not make anything of a kind so that it be known whether it is from an origin returning to its essence, or from the management of a number each doing a direction, thus conflicting with each being unique in the direction that is from it. And there is no power except through God. Also, the entities are seen under the limit of all bodies, and they are combined upon opposing natures, while their right is to repel and separate due to the enmity between them, such that if one imagined leaving them to their natures, the corruption of the whole would result. So it is established that the manager of all between them is one; He brings them together with gentleness, and restrains the harm of each from the other with amazing wisdom that imaginations cannot reach. And if it were due to a number, the truth of disagreement and opposition would run in them, according to what the will of the agents [requires] from repelling others and from the making of others so that His making becomes clear. And with God is deliverance. And it is possible to combine the two aspects in all that the consideration ends at from the indication that it emerges upon looking at the states and acts. The states: that they be equal in all meanings of lordship, so in that there would be repulsion and prevention, since that was the description of an individual they call number, or they differ, so the most perfect of them would be more entitled to lordship. As for the acts: what I mentioned of the harmony of the entire world despite the contradiction of natures and their opposition, they become as if they are forms in the subsistence of some by some, and some being for some a help and supporter in survival. And if they were in the way I mentioned, it is established that that harmony with opposition is not possible except through a wise, knowing, gentle Manager, who is not disputed in management, nor opposed in determination, and there is no power except through God.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part proof of divine unity (tawḥīd) from the observable order and coherence of the world. Maturidi presents several arguments, each building on the harmony of creation despite diversity and opposition.

First argument: The distribution of needs and livelihoods across all regions, and the interlocking times (day and night, seasons) that follow a measured pattern, point to a single provider and manager. If there were multiple gods, it would be impossible for the resources to originate from one source without conflict. Maturidi cites Quran 67:3 as evidence that there is no disparity in creation.

Second argument (introduced by 'فهذا'): Bodies are created on six directions (dimensions) and yet are unified under one meaning, necessitating a single manager.

Third argument: No atom is purely harmful or beneficial, good or bad; things change in different contexts. This mixture of qualities across all things shows that no object is fixed in its nature, which would be expected if it came from a single essence or from multiple directorial forces each imposing a fixed character. The fact that everything has varying opposites indicates a single director who balances all aspects.

Fourth argument: Entities exist under the category of bodies and possess opposing natures; their natural tendency is conflict and dissolution. Yet we see them coexisting and supporting each other. This survival cannot happen without a single wise manager who restrains harm and preserves order. If there were multiple gods, their natural opposition would lead to chaos.

Fifth argument: Considering the states (aḥwāl) and acts (afʿāl) of gods if there were multiple: either they are equal in lordship, leading to mutual opposition, or one is superior, and the superior alone deserves lordship. The actual harmony of the world, with its many opposing forces working together, cannot be the result of multiple agents but only of a single, wise, all-knowing, and gentle manager who has no rival in determination.

Key Terms
جهات ست (jihāt sitt)
جوهر (jawhar)
مدبر (mudabbir)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Atoms or objects have fixed inherent natures that come from different sources.
Correction: Maturidi observes that qualities are not fixed; the same thing can be good or bad in different contexts, indicating a single source that blends them rather than multiple sources with fixed natures.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi argue about atoms (jawhar)?
A) Each atom is purely good or purely evil.
B) No atom is purely harmful or beneficial; qualities are relative.
C) Atoms are eternal.
D) Atoms are managed by multiple gods.

Key Takeaway
The unity of all bodies under one meaning and the relativity of qualities in all atoms both prove a single Director.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience something painful or harmful, do you tend to assume it is purely negative, or do you pause to consider how it might become good in a different context? What would change in your heart if you truly believed that no atom is purely harmful and that all is directed by one wise Manager?
?
The passage argues that the diversity of qualities (bad/good, blessing/trial) points to one Director, not multiple conflicting forces. Reflect on a trial you are facing right now. Can you see how it might be part of a single coherent plan? If so, what is your response to the Director? If not, what would it take for you to trust that He is one?
?
Your life is composed of countless 'atoms'—moments, experiences, relationships—each with mixed qualities. Are you living as though these are random and contradictory, or as though they are gathered under one meaning by a single Director? Make a concrete commitment today to change one way you react to life's mixture of harms and benefits.

The Coexistence of Opposing Natures Proves One Manager
Maturidi's argument from the harmony of opposing natures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that bodies with mutually repelling natures can only coexist through a single wise manager who restrains their harm.

Core Idea
The natural enmity of opposites would destroy all; only a single wise being can harmonize them.

Maturidi now presents a striking argument: all entities in the world possess opposing natures (ṭabāʿiʿ mutaḍādda) that naturally repel each other. If left to themselves, they would clash and cause the corruption of the whole. Yet we see them coexisting and even supporting each other's survival. This is impossible without a single manager who restrains harm with wisdom and brings them together with gentleness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Identify the contradiction Maturidi highlights.
2
Understand the natural opposition
Maturidi says bodies have opposing natures, and their right is to repel and separate. This leads to enmity.
Think of fire and water, predator and prey, etc.
3
Imagining the alternative
If left to their natures, the corruption of the whole would result. Imagine what would happen without a restraining force.
4
Conclude the argument
The fact that they coexist proves one manager who restrains harm. If there were multiple gods, their own opposition would cause chaos.

The Impossibility of Multiple Gods: States and Acts
Maturidi's final synthesizing argument from the states and acts of multiple gods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's final argument that whether multiple gods are equal or unequal, the result is impossible, and only a single wise manager can explain the world's order.

Core Idea
Equality leads to conflict; inequality leads to the superior deserving sole lordship; harmony demands one God.

In this concluding passage, Maturidi sums up his arguments by considering the hypothetical states and acts of multiple gods. If they were equal in lordship, they would repel each other; if unequal, the most perfect would be the true lord. Moreover, the observed harmony of the world despite contradictory natures can only come from a single wise manager who is not disputed in management. This final argument reinforces the previous ones by showing that the very structure of reasoning leads to tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the two aspects: states (aḥwāl) and acts (afʿāl).
2
Analyze the states argument
Maturidi says if multiple gods are equal in all meanings of lordship, there would be repulsion and prevention. If they differ, the most perfect is more entitled to lordship.
This is a classic argument of the impossibility of two omnipotent beings.
3
Analyze the acts argument
The harmony of the world with its contradictory natures is like forms supporting each other. This cannot happen unless there is one manager.
Maturidi refers back to his earlier arguments about nature.
4
Synthesize the conclusion
Both approaches—states and acts—lead to the same conclusion: a single, wise, knowing, gentle Manager, with no rival.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع يكون بأسباب السماء و حاجات كل أهل البلدان منتشرة في جميع الأطراف، ومعاش البشر مجعول في أنواع المكاسب؛ على هذا دار أمر الجميع. فلو كان ذلك لعدد ، لم يحتمل أن ترجع منابعها إلى من له العالم من الخلق ، على اختلاف العالم؛ ثبت أن مدبر ذلك كله واحد. وعلى ما ذكرت الأوقات من الليل والنهار والساعات، ودخول بعض في بعض على قدر الحاجات، وهذا ـ والله أعلم - معنى قوله : ما ترى في خلق الرحمن من تفاوت [الملك، ٣/٦٧]. فهذا، ما جعلت الأجسام، وهي الأعيان على جهات ست. ثبت أن مدبر كل على اختلاف الأجناس واحد، حتى جمع الكل تحت معنى واحد. ولا قوة إلا بالله. والثالث أنه لا يُوجد جوهر واحد يرجع بجوهره إلى معنى واحد من الضرر أو النفع، أو الخبث أو الطيب، أو النعمة أو البلاء، بل كل شيء يوصف بالخبث فهو يصير طيبا في وجه ولغير من له خبث، وكذلك سائر الصفات. وعلى ذلك أحوال الأشياء: إنها ليست على نفع بكل حال أو ضرر بكل حال. ثبت أن مدير ذلك كله واحد، حتى جمع في كل وجوه المضار والمنافع، ولم يجعل شيئا ذا نوع ليُعلم أنه عن أصل يرجع إلى جوهره، أو عن تدبير عدد يفعل كل جهة فيتناقض بما تفرد كل بالجهة التي هي منه . ولا قوة إلا بالله . وأيضا إن الأعيان تراها تحت حد الأجسام كلها، وهي مجتمعة على طبائع متضادة، حقها التنافر والتباعد بما بينها من التعادى الذي لو توهم تركها وطباعها لكان في ذلك فساد الكل. فثبت أن مدبر الجميع بينها واحد ؛ يجمعهم باللطف، ويحبس ضرر كل عن غيره بالحكمة العجيبة التي لا تبلغها الأوهام. ولو كان لعددٍ لجرى فيها حق الاختلاف والتضاد، على ما عليه إرادة الفاعلين من السد بغيرهم وبصنع غيرهم ليتبين صنعه. وبالله النجاة. وأمكن الجمع بين الحرفين في جميع ما ينتهي إليه الاعتبار من الإشارة إلى الدلالة أنها تخرج على النظر إلى الأحوال والأفعال. فالأحوال هي أن يكونوا في جميع معاني الربوبية سواء، فيكون في ذلك تدافع وتمانع مع ما كان ذلك صفة فردٍ سموه عددًا، أو تختلف ، فيكون الأتمّ لها أحق بالربوبية. وأما الأفعال فما ذكرتُ من اتساق جميع العالم مع تناقض الطبائع وتضادها صارت كأنها أشكال في قوام بعض ببعض، وكون بعض لبعض عونا و ناصرا في البقاء. وإن كانوا بالوجه الذي ذكرت ثبت أن ذلك التألف مع التضاد لا يُحتمل إلا بمدبر حكيم عليم لطيف، لا ينازع في التدبير، ولا يُخالف في التقدير ولا قوة إلا بالله .
With the causes of the sky and the needs of all the people of the lands being spread in all regions, and the livelihood of humanity made in various types of earnings; upon this the whole matter revolves. So if that were due to a number [of gods], it would not be possible for their sources to return to the one who [alone] has the world from among the creation, despite the diversity of the world; it is established that the manager of all that is one. And according to what is mentioned of the times of night and day and the hours, and the interpenetration of one into another according to needs, and this — and God knows best — is the meaning of His saying: ‘You see not in the creation of the Most Merciful any disparity’ [Q. 67:3]. So this, that bodies — which are the entities — were made on six directions. It is established that the manager of everything despite the diversity of kinds is one, until He gathered the whole under one meaning. And there is no power except through God. And the third: that there is not found a single atom that returns in its essence to one meaning of harm or benefit, or bad or good, or blessing or trial; rather, everything described as bad becomes good in some aspect and for other than the one who has badness, and likewise the rest of the attributes. Upon that are the states of things: they are not [entirely] beneficial in every case or harmful in every case. It is established that the director of all that is one, until He gathered in all aspects of harms and benefits, and did not make anything of a kind so that it be known whether it is from an origin returning to its essence, or from the management of a number each doing a direction, thus conflicting with each being unique in the direction that is from it. And there is no power except through God. Also, the entities are seen under the limit of all bodies, and they are combined upon opposing natures, while their right is to repel and separate due to the enmity between them, such that if one imagined leaving them to their natures, the corruption of the whole would result. So it is established that the manager of all between them is one; He brings them together with gentleness, and restrains the harm of each from the other with amazing wisdom that imaginations cannot reach. And if it were due to a number, the truth of disagreement and opposition would run in them, according to what the will of the agents [requires] from repelling others and from the making of others so that His making becomes clear. And with God is deliverance. And it is possible to combine the two aspects in all that the consideration ends at from the indication that it emerges upon looking at the states and acts. The states: that they be equal in all meanings of lordship, so in that there would be repulsion and prevention, since that was the description of an individual they call number, or they differ, so the most perfect of them would be more entitled to lordship. As for the acts: what I mentioned of the harmony of the entire world despite the contradiction of natures and their opposition, they become as if they are forms in the subsistence of some by some, and some being for some a help and supporter in survival. And if they were in the way I mentioned, it is established that that harmony with opposition is not possible except through a wise, knowing, gentle Manager, who is not disputed in management, nor opposed in determination, and there is no power except through God.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part proof of divine unity (tawḥīd) from the observable order and coherence of the world. Maturidi presents several arguments, each building on the harmony of creation despite diversity and opposition.

First argument: The distribution of needs and livelihoods across all regions, and the interlocking times (day and night, seasons) that follow a measured pattern, point to a single provider and manager. If there were multiple gods, it would be impossible for the resources to originate from one source without conflict. Maturidi cites Quran 67:3 as evidence that there is no disparity in creation.

Second argument (introduced by 'فهذا'): Bodies are created on six directions (dimensions) and yet are unified under one meaning, necessitating a single manager.

Third argument: No atom is purely harmful or beneficial, good or bad; things change in different contexts. This mixture of qualities across all things shows that no object is fixed in its nature, which would be expected if it came from a single essence or from multiple directorial forces each imposing a fixed character. The fact that everything has varying opposites indicates a single director who balances all aspects.

Fourth argument: Entities exist under the category of bodies and possess opposing natures; their natural tendency is conflict and dissolution. Yet we see them coexisting and supporting each other. This survival cannot happen without a single wise manager who restrains harm and preserves order. If there were multiple gods, their natural opposition would lead to chaos.

Fifth argument: Considering the states (aḥwāl) and acts (afʿāl) of gods if there were multiple: either they are equal in lordship, leading to mutual opposition, or one is superior, and the superior alone deserves lordship. The actual harmony of the world, with its many opposing forces working together, cannot be the result of multiple agents but only of a single, wise, all-knowing, and gentle manager who has no rival in determination.

Key Terms
أحوال وأفعال (aḥwāl wa afʿāl)
ربوبية (rubūbiyya)
تدبير (tadbīr)
تقدير (taqdīr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Multiple gods could be arranged in a hierarchy with the most perfect ruling and others subordinate, thus explaining order.
Correction: Maturidi argues that if they are unequal, the most perfect alone is entitled to lordship; the others cannot be gods. Moreover, harmony despite opposition requires a single manager, not a hierarchy.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what happens if multiple gods are equal in all meanings of lordship?
A) They would cooperate harmoniously.
B) There would be repulsion and prevention.
C) The most perfect would rule.
D) They would divide the world.

Key Takeaway
Whether considered in terms of equal or unequal lordship, or the harmony of the world, multiple gods are impossible; only one wise manager can explain the universe.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that the world's harmony requires a single wise Manager, then why do you still turn to other sources—people, wealth, or your own plans—as if they have independent control? What would it look like this week to rely solely on that one Manager?
?
When you observe the complexity and opposition in nature—sickness and health, life and death—do you see them as random or as part of a unified plan? How does this lesson challenge you to trust that plan even when you don't understand it?
?
Consider any area of your life where you act as if there are multiple 'lords'—your career, relationships, or desires. In light of this passage’s argument that only the most perfect deserves lordship, are you willing to dethrone those lesser lords and submit to the one true Manager? What is holding you back?

The Error of Anthropomorphists and the Muslim Stance
Maturidi identifies two anthropomorphist groups and states the Muslim position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's critique of two anthropomorphist groups and the Muslim response of affirming God's 'that-ness' while negating all creaturely attributes.

Core Idea
Anthropomorphism arises from projecting worldly concepts onto God; Muslims must affirm God's distinct existence without attributes of creation.

Maturidi begins by showing that the attributes we know from creation are understood differently when applied to God. He then identifies two misguided groups among those who liken God to creation. One group denies the Creator entirely, and the other makes God subject to events. Muslims, by contrast, affirm God's unique that-ness and negate all creaturely limitations.

Guided Path
1
Read the critique
Read the passage where Maturidi describes the obstinacy of anthropomorphists and enumerates the two groups. Notice how he connects their error to the cause of atheism.
The passage begins with 'ويوصف به من الصفات' and ends with 'ونفوا عنه جميع ما احتمل غيره'.
2
Identify the two groups
The passage lists two specific sects: those who make God an entity and deny the Maker, and those who make Him susceptible to events. Understand what each group claims and how they differ.
The second group is called 'ashab al-hayula' (materialists).
3
Study the Muslim response
The Muslims affirm God's 'huwiyya' (that-ness) necessarily and negate everything that creation admits. Note the list of negated qualities: differentiation, change, increase, decrease.
This negation preserves God's transcendence.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Ask yourself: Why is it necessary to negate these creaturely attributes from God? What does this tell us about His transcendence?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويوصف به من الصفات بما يُفهم منه لو أضيف إلى الخلق ووصف به. وبالله التوفيق. وفي ذلك ظهور تعنت المشبهة ، وذلك سبب إلحاد من ألحد؛ إنه ظن به ما احتمله الشاهد. فمنهم من جعله أحد الأعيان وأنكر الصانع للعالم وادعى أنه على ما عليه [في الأزل]. ومنهم من صيّره محتملا للحوادث وأنكر حَدَثَه وزعم أن غيره حوادث اعترضت بقوته ، وهم أصحاب الهيولى . والمسلمون لزمهم القول بهستيته ضرورة فقالوا [به] ونفوا عنه جميع ما احتمل غيره ، إذ احتمل غيره التفاضل في الذوات والاختلاف في الصفات، أو احتمل غيره الاستحالة والتغير بما يتمكن فيه الزيادة والنقصان، وإن كان بعض ذلك ثوابت فهو نوع المحتمل لذلك. على أن ثباته بالتسخير على ما هو عليه من دوام الحركة أو السكون، أو باحتمال التضاد الذي هو آفة الموجود بما فيه احتمال الفناء، ووجود الأشباه له ليبطل عنه صفة الكمال والتمام، أو تمكن النهاية له والحد الذي يتوهم معه الأتمّ والأنقص، والأوفر والأقصر، فهذه الوجوه من آيات حدث العالم وأدلة مُحدثه. فلو كان لمحدثه [بعض الصفات] مما به عُرِفَ حَدَث العالم وأن له مُحدثا ليلحقه من ذلك الوجه ما [لحق] غيره، و فيه فساد العالم وشهادتِهِ على مُحْدِث حكيم عليم متعال عن الأشباه والأضداد. مع ما كان كل [شيء] غير له حدث من جميع الوجوه، فلو كان لشيء منه شَبَه يَسقط عنه من ذلك القِدَمُ ، أو عن غيره الحدث. ولا قوة إلا بالله. على أن الشبه من كل جهة في الخلق ممتنع لما يصير واحدا، وإنما يكون في جهة دون جهة، فلو وصف بالشبه بغيره بجهة فيصير من ذلك الوجه كأحد الخلق من الخلق، إذ ذلك التشابه بينهم . ولا قوة إلا بالله.
He is described with attributes that would be understood if attributed to creation and described thereby. And with Allah is success. And in that appears the obstinacy of the anthropomorphists, and that is the cause of atheism of whoever becomes atheist; indeed he thought about Him what the witnessed (al-shahid) admits. Among them are those who made Him one of the entities and denied the Maker of the world and claimed that He is as He was [in eternity]. And among them are those who made Him susceptible to events and denied His temporality and claimed that other than Him are events that occur by His power, and they are the proponents of hyle (ashab al-hayula). And the Muslims were obliged to affirm His 'that-ness' (huwiyya) necessarily, so they affirmed [it] and negated from Him everything that other than Him admits, since other than Him admits differentiation in essences and difference in attributes, or other than Him admits change and alteration involving increase and decrease, and if some of that is stable, it is a type of what admits that. Because His stability is by subjugation (taskhir) as it is of perpetual motion or rest, or by admitting opposition which is the affliction of the existent including the possibility of annihilation, and the existence of likenesses to Him would nullify His attribute of perfection and completeness, or the possibility of an end for Him and a limit by which one imagines the more perfect and the less perfect, and the more abundant and the shorter. So these aspects are signs of the temporality of the world and proofs of its efficient cause. So if its efficient cause had [some attributes] by which the temporality of the world and that it has an efficient cause are known, then by that aspect what [affects] other than Him would affect Him, and in it is the corruption of the world and its testifying to a wise, knowing efficient cause transcendent over likenesses and opposites. Since everything [other] than Him is temporal in all aspects, if anything of it had a likeness, then eternity would drop from that, or temporality from other than it. And there is no power except with Allah. Moreover, likeness in every respect among creatures is impossible because it would make them one; rather it is in one respect without another. So if He were described by likeness to other than Him in one respect, He would become in that respect like one of creation from creation, since that similarity is between them. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the temporality (huduth) of the world and a refutation of those who liken God to creation (mushabbiha) and materialists (dahriyya). Maturidi begins by stating that attributes understood from creation, when applied to God, are understood differently. He then identifies two groups of anthropomorphists: those who consider God a physical entity and deny the Creator, and those who make Him subject to events (hawadith) while denying His own temporality, claiming that events arise from His power—these are the materialists (ashab al-hayula). Muslims, by necessity, affirm God's 'that-ness' (huwiyya) and negate from Him all that creation admits, such as differentiation in essences, change, increase and decrease. Even stable things are still contingent. Maturidi then argues that the world's stability is by subjugation (taskhir) and involves motion or rest, opposition (tadadd), possibility of annihilation, and likenesses that would negate perfection—all signs of temporality. These aspects are proofs of the world's having an efficient cause (muhdith). If that efficient cause had attributes by which the world's temporality is known, then it would be subject to the same contingencies. The corruption of the world itself testifies to a wise, knowing efficient cause transcendent over likenesses and opposites. Since everything other than God is temporal in all respects, if anything had a likeness to God, that thing would lose its temporality or God would lose His eternity. Likeness in every respect among creatures is impossible because it would make them identical; likeness only occurs in some respect. If God were described as like another in any respect, He would become like that creature in that respect.

Key Terms
المشبهة
الدهرية
أصحاب الهيولى
الهستية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that affirming attributes for God necessarily implies He resembles creation.
Correction: Maturidi argues that attributes are known through the witnessed world but negate any actual similarity; Muslims affirm God's unique 'that-ness' and negate all creaturely qualities.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what do the 'ashab al-hayula' claim?
A) God is a physical entity and the world is eternal.
B) God is susceptible to events but not temporal, and events occur by His power.
C) God is a body with parts.
D) God does not exist.

Key Takeaway
Anthropomorphism leads to atheism if God is likened to creation; Muslims affirm God's unique that-ness and negate all creaturely qualities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever realized that your own mental image of Allah might include subtle limitations or human-like traits? In light of this lesson, what specific thought patterns do you need to repent from?
?
When you think about Allah, do you focus more on what He is not (e.g., not like creation) than on affirming His unique that-ness? How can you shift your worship to a positive affirmation of His reality?
?
The materialists denied God because they projected worldly concepts onto Him. Where in your daily life do you project worldly expectations onto Allah, such as expecting instant answers or specific outcomes? How will you guard against this?

Signs of the World's Temporality
Maturidi enumerates six signs proving the world's temporality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six signs Maturidi presents as proof of the world's temporality and its dependence on a Creator.

Core Idea
The world’s constant change and limitations are clear signs that it is created and not eternal.

After establishing the Muslim position, Maturidi provides a series of arguments demonstrating that the world is temporal (hadith). These focus on the contingent nature of the world: its stability is enforced (taskhir), it involves motion or rest, it admits opposition and annihilation, it has likenesses, and it has limits. All these point to a Creator who is beyond such limitations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on signs
Read from 'على أن ثباته بالتسخير' to 'فهذه الوجوه من آيات حدث العالم وأدلة مُحدثه'. Note each sign listed.
The passage enumerates six signs.
2
Identify the six signs
The passage lists six aspects: stability by subjugation, perpetual motion or rest, possibility of opposition, possibility of annihilation, existence of likenesses, and possibility of an end with degrees. Understand how each indicates temporality.
Each sign shows the world is not self-sufficient.
3
Connect to the proof
Maturidi concludes these are signs of the world's temporality and proofs of its efficient cause. Reflect on how each sign necessitates a creator.
4
Ponder the implications
If the world has these signs, what does that imply about its Creator? He must be free from all such contingencies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويوصف به من الصفات بما يُفهم منه لو أضيف إلى الخلق ووصف به. وبالله التوفيق. وفي ذلك ظهور تعنت المشبهة ، وذلك سبب إلحاد من ألحد؛ إنه ظن به ما احتمله الشاهد. فمنهم من جعله أحد الأعيان وأنكر الصانع للعالم وادعى أنه على ما عليه [في الأزل]. ومنهم من صيّره محتملا للحوادث وأنكر حَدَثَه وزعم أن غيره حوادث اعترضت بقوته ، وهم أصحاب الهيولى . والمسلمون لزمهم القول بهستيته ضرورة فقالوا [به] ونفوا عنه جميع ما احتمل غيره ، إذ احتمل غيره التفاضل في الذوات والاختلاف في الصفات، أو احتمل غيره الاستحالة والتغير بما يتمكن فيه الزيادة والنقصان، وإن كان بعض ذلك ثوابت فهو نوع المحتمل لذلك. على أن ثباته بالتسخير على ما هو عليه من دوام الحركة أو السكون، أو باحتمال التضاد الذي هو آفة الموجود بما فيه احتمال الفناء، ووجود الأشباه له ليبطل عنه صفة الكمال والتمام، أو تمكن النهاية له والحد الذي يتوهم معه الأتمّ والأنقص، والأوفر والأقصر، فهذه الوجوه من آيات حدث العالم وأدلة مُحدثه. فلو كان لمحدثه [بعض الصفات] مما به عُرِفَ حَدَث العالم وأن له مُحدثا ليلحقه من ذلك الوجه ما [لحق] غيره، و فيه فساد العالم وشهادتِهِ على مُحْدِث حكيم عليم متعال عن الأشباه والأضداد. مع ما كان كل [شيء] غير له حدث من جميع الوجوه، فلو كان لشيء منه شَبَه يَسقط عنه من ذلك القِدَمُ ، أو عن غيره الحدث. ولا قوة إلا بالله. على أن الشبه من كل جهة في الخلق ممتنع لما يصير واحدا، وإنما يكون في جهة دون جهة، فلو وصف بالشبه بغيره بجهة فيصير من ذلك الوجه كأحد الخلق من الخلق، إذ ذلك التشابه بينهم . ولا قوة إلا بالله.

Maturidi begins by stating that attributes understood from creation, when applied to God, are understood differently. He then identifies two groups of anthropomorphists: those who consider God a physical entity and deny the Creator, and those who make Him subject to events (hawadith) while denying His own temporality, claiming that events arise from His power—these are the materialists (ashab al-hayula). Muslims, by necessity, affirm God's 'that-ness' (huwiyya) and negate from Him all that creation admits, such as differentiation in essences, change, increase and decrease. Even stable things are still contingent. Maturidi then argues that the world's stability is by subjugation (taskhir) and involves motion or rest, opposition (tadadd), possibility of annihilation, and likenesses that would negate perfection—all signs of temporality. These aspects are proofs of the world's having an efficient cause (muhdith). If that efficient cause had attributes by which the world's temporality is known, then it would be subject to the same contingencies. The corruption of the world itself testifies to a wise, knowing efficient cause transcendent over likenesses and opposites. Since everything other than God is temporal in all respects, if anything had a likeness to God, that thing would lose its temporality or God would lose His eternity. Likeness in every respect among creatures is impossible because it would make them identical; likeness only occurs in some respect. If God were described as like another in any respect, He would become like that creature in that respect.

Key Terms
التسخير
التضاد
الشبه
الحدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the world's regular patterns indicate eternity.
Correction: Maturidi argues that these regularities (motion, rest, opposition, etc.) are contingent signs of temporality, not eternity.

Checkpoint

A) Stability by subjugation
B) Likenesses
C) Eternity
D) Opposition

Key Takeaway
The world's dependence, change, and limitations are clear proofs that it had a beginning and a Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The sixth sign mentions that the world has ends and limits, implying degrees of perfection. If you could only achieve a 'less perfect' version of something you desire, would you still be content? What does your answer say about your trust in Allah's wisdom and the sufficiency of what He has decreed?

The Impossibility of Likeness Between Creator and Creation
Maturidi argues against any divine-creature likeness using logical conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that if God had any likeness to creation, it would undermine His eternity and perfection, and why absolute likeness among creatures is impossible.

Core Idea
If God were like any creature in any respect, He would cease to be the unique, eternal Creator.

Maturidi concludes his argument by addressing the issue of likeness (shabah). He argues that if God had a likeness in one aspect, He would become like that creature in that aspect, which is impossible for the Creator. Moreover, perfect likeness among creatures would make them identical, so likeness is always partial. Therefore, God must be absolutely transcendent.

Guided Path
1
Read the final argument
Read from 'فلو كان لمحدثه' to the end of the lesson. Pay attention to the conditional reasoning about likeness.
This is the most advanced part of the passage.
2
Analyze the conditional
Maturidi says if the efficient cause had attributes that reveal temporality, it would be subject to the same. Understand why that would corrupt the world's testimony.
The world's corruption points to a transcendent Maker.
3
Examine the point on likeness
He states that if anything had a likeness to God, eternity would drop from it or temporality from the other. This absolute disjunction shows the impossibility.
4
Consider the nature of likeness among creatures
Likeness in every respect is impossible because it would make them one. Likeness is always partial. So if God were described as like another in any respect, He would become like that creature.
5
Conclude the lesson
Now you see why Maturidi insists on God's absolute transcendence: any resemblance would contradict His divinity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويوصف به من الصفات بما يُفهم منه لو أضيف إلى الخلق ووصف به. وبالله التوفيق. وفي ذلك ظهور تعنت المشبهة ، وذلك سبب إلحاد من ألحد؛ إنه ظن به ما احتمله الشاهد. فمنهم من جعله أحد الأعيان وأنكر الصانع للعالم وادعى أنه على ما عليه [في الأزل]. ومنهم من صيّره محتملا للحوادث وأنكر حَدَثَه وزعم أن غيره حوادث اعترضت بقوته ، وهم أصحاب الهيولى . والمسلمون لزمهم القول بهستيته ضرورة فقالوا [به] ونفوا عنه جميع ما احتمل غيره ، إذ احتمل غيره التفاضل في الذوات والاختلاف في الصفات، أو احتمل غيره الاستحالة والتغير بما يتمكن فيه الزيادة والنقصان، وإن كان بعض ذلك ثوابت فهو نوع المحتمل لذلك. على أن ثباته بالتسخير على ما هو عليه من دوام الحركة أو السكون، أو باحتمال التضاد الذي هو آفة الموجود بما فيه احتمال الفناء، ووجود الأشباه له ليبطل عنه صفة الكمال والتمام، أو تمكن النهاية له والحد الذي يتوهم معه الأتمّ والأنقص، والأوفر والأقصر، فهذه الوجوه من آيات حدث العالم وأدلة مُحدثه. فلو كان لمحدثه [بعض الصفات] مما به عُرِفَ حَدَث العالم وأن له مُحدثا ليلحقه من ذلك الوجه ما [لحق] غيره، و فيه فساد العالم وشهادتِهِ على مُحْدِث حكيم عليم متعال عن الأشباه والأضداد. مع ما كان كل [شيء] غير له حدث من جميع الوجوه، فلو كان لشيء منه شَبَه يَسقط عنه من ذلك القِدَمُ ، أو عن غيره الحدث. ولا قوة إلا بالله. على أن الشبه من كل جهة في الخلق ممتنع لما يصير واحدا، وإنما يكون في جهة دون جهة، فلو وصف بالشبه بغيره بجهة فيصير من ذلك الوجه كأحد الخلق من الخلق، إذ ذلك التشابه بينهم . ولا قوة إلا بالله.
He is described with attributes that would be understood if attributed to creation and described thereby. And with Allah is success. And in that appears the obstinacy of the anthropomorphists, and that is the cause of atheism of whoever becomes atheist; indeed he thought about Him what the witnessed (al-shahid) admits. Among them are those who made Him one of the entities and denied the Maker of the world and claimed that He is as He was [in eternity]. And among them are those who made Him susceptible to events and denied His temporality and claimed that other than Him are events that occur by His power, and they are the proponents of hyle (ashab al-hayula). And the Muslims were obliged to affirm His 'that-ness' (huwiyya) necessarily, so they affirmed [it] and negated from Him everything that other than Him admits, since other than Him admits differentiation in essences and difference in attributes, or other than Him admits change and alteration involving increase and decrease, and if some of that is stable, it is a type of what admits that. Because His stability is by subjugation (taskhir) as it is of perpetual motion or rest, or by admitting opposition which is the affliction of the existent including the possibility of annihilation, and the existence of likenesses to Him would nullify His attribute of perfection and completeness, or the possibility of an end for Him and a limit by which one imagines the more perfect and the less perfect, and the more abundant and the shorter. So these aspects are signs of the temporality of the world and proofs of its efficient cause. So if its efficient cause had [some attributes] by which the temporality of the world and that it has an efficient cause are known, then by that aspect what [affects] other than Him would affect Him, and in it is the corruption of the world and its testifying to a wise, knowing efficient cause transcendent over likenesses and opposites. Since everything [other] than Him is temporal in all aspects, if anything of it had a likeness, then eternity would drop from that, or temporality from other than it. And there is no power except with Allah. Moreover, likeness in every respect among creatures is impossible because it would make them one; rather it is in one respect without another. So if He were described by likeness to other than Him in one respect, He would become in that respect like one of creation from creation, since that similarity is between them. And there is no power except with Allah.

This passage is a proof for the temporality (huduth) of the world and a refutation of those who liken God to creation (mushabbiha) and materialists (dahriyya). Likeness in every respect among creatures is impossible because it would make them identical; likeness only occurs in some respect. If God were described as like another in any respect, He would become like that creature in that respect.

The Corruption of the World as Proof of a Transcendent Creator
Maturidi argues from the corruption of the world to the existence and transcendence of the Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the corruption of the world to prove a Creator who is absolutely transcendent, without any likeness to creation.

Core Idea
The world's very imperfection points to a perfect Creator beyond all comparison.

Imam Maturidi begins by grounding theological proof in the observable world. The corruption (fasād) of the world is not a flaw but a sign—it shows that the world is not self-sufficient and requires a Maker. Yet this Maker cannot be like His creation. In this short passage, Maturidi weaves together two arguments: one from contingency and one from the impossibility of likeness between Creator and creature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage closely
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the repeated phrase 'La quwwata illa billah' which frames the argument.
2
Follow the conditional argument
Maturidi presents a conditional: if a created thing had a likeness (shabah) to God, then either that thing would become pre-eternal or God would become temporal—both impossible. Trace this logic carefully.
This is a concise demonstration of divine transcendence (tanzih).
3
Understand the second argument on likeness
Maturidi adds that likeness in every respect would collapse two things into one, which is impossible. Likeness can only occur in some aspects, but even that would make the thing resemble other created things, not the Creator.
This reinforces the absolute uniqueness of God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فساد العالم وشهادتِهِ على مُحْدِث حكيم عليم متعال عن الأشباه والأضداد. مع ما كان كل غير له حدث من جميع الوجوه، فلو كان لشيء منه شَبَه يَسقط عنه من ذلك القِدَمُ، أو عن غيره الحدث. ولا قوة إلا بالله. على أن الشبه من كل جهة في الخلق ممتنع لما يصير واحدا، وإنما يكون في جهة دون جهة، فلو وصف بالشبه بغيره بجهة فيصير من ذلك الوجه كأحد الخلق من الخلق، إذ ذلك التشابه بينهم. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
The corruption of the world and its testimony to a Maker, Wise, Knowing, transcendent above likenesses and opposites. Since everything other than Him is temporally originated in all aspects, so if something of it had a likeness (shabah) to Him, then pre-eternity (qidam) would drop from it, or temporal origination (hadath) would drop from the other. And there is no power save with God. Moreover, likeness in every respect in creation is impossible because it would become one [and the same], and it only occurs in one aspect without another. So if something is described as similar to another in some aspect, it becomes in that aspect like one of the created things from creation, since that similarity is between them. And there is no power save with God.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a proof (istidlal) from the corruption of the world to the existence of a Creator who is wise, knowing, and absolutely transcendent. Maturidi begins by stating that the world’s corruption and its characteristics testify to a Maker who is above all likenesses and contrasts. He then makes a key argument: everything besides God is temporally originated (hadith) in all respects. If any created thing possessed a likeness (shabah) to God in any attribute that is specific to God (such as pre-eternity), then that thing would become eternal, or alternatively God would become temporal—both impossible. Thus, no likeness can exist. He further explains that likeness in every aspect would collapse two distinct entities into one, which is absurd. Likeness can only occur in one aspect without the other, but even then, that aspect would make the thing resemble created things, which is not suitable for God. This establishes the principle of divine transcendence (tanzih).

Key Terms

محدث
شبه
قدم
حدث
تشابه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Maturidi denies any relationship between Creator and creation, such as causality or attributes.
Correction: Maturidi only denies likeness (shabah) between Creator and creation, not existence or attributes. He affirms that the world points to a Maker, but that Maker is beyond comparison.

Key Takeaway
The corruption of the world proves a Creator who is absolutely transcendent, with no likeness to creation.

How will you actively train your mind to think of God as beyond all comparison? Start by listing one assumption you must abandon.

Refuting the Origin-Branch Argument
Refutes the origin-branch argument and explains the external nature of created things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Eternal cannot be considered a branch of the temporal and how all created things are external to the essence of their agent.

Core Idea
The Eternal was not derived from the temporal; rather the temporal depends on the Eternal.

Māturīdī tackles a flawed argument that tries to make the seen world the 'origin' and the unseen God the 'branch.' He flips this logic, showing that the Eternal and pre-eternity existed before any inference, so the unseen is the true origin. This lesson unpacks that inversion and the principle that products are external to their maker's essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read both the Arabic and the literal translation. Pay attention to the logical flow: first the claim is stated, then reversed.
Notice the phrase 'فمقلوب' — 'is inverted' — signals the correction.
2
Identify the key claim and its refutation
The opponents claim the seen is the origin (aṣl) and the unseen the branch (farʿ). Find how Māturīdī refutes this by pointing to the pre-existence of the Eternal.
The Eternal (al-Qadīm) and pre-eternity (al-qidam) existed before any means of inference.
3
Understand the 'external to essence' principle
The passage states that things which come into existence through an agent are external to the agent's essence. Examples: building, writing. This prevents attributing the product's qualities to the agent.
This principle is crucial for avoiding anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما زعم من الأصل والفرع فمقلوب؛ لما كان القديم والقدم ولم يكن ما به استدل، فلذلك لم يجب جعله فرعا لهذا، بل هو الأصل لكون هذا به. ثم كل كائن بغيره، من طريق العقل، خارج عن جوهره في الشاهد، كالبناء والكتابة وكل أنواع الأفعال والأقوال التي هي أغيار لمن كنّ بهم، لم يجز أن يلحقهم بالجوهر والصفة، فمثله الذي به العالم. على أنه جاز في الشاهد إثبات ما لا يُدرك ولا يُحاط به نحو السمع والبصر والروح والعقل والهوى ونحو ذلك، وما يُدْرَك نحو الأجسام الكثيفة؛ فلو كانت هي قديمة الأصل فيجب أن يكون كل نوع يتولد ويحدث من جوهره: العقل من العقل، وكذلك البصر والسمع. ومعلوم الاختلاف بين كل جوهر والمتولّد منه في ذلك؛ فلزم الكون والحدث إن كان مختلفا، وفي تثبيت الاختلاف بطلان أن يكون الذي في وصف القدم عالما، أو على ما عليه صفته، وفي ذلك إثبات حدث العالم بمن ليس كمثله. وبعد، فإن الكتابة تدل على الكاتب ، ولا تدل على كيفيته أو مثله ، لما يجوز أن يكون مَلَكًا أو بشراً أو جنّاً، فتكون الكتابة غير دالة على مائية الكاتب وكيفيته ولا على مثلها، وهي تدل على كاتب ما . فمثله العالم بما فيه يدل على مُحْدِث ما ولا يدل على كيفيته ومائيته، وكذلك البناء والنَّسيج والنَّجْر والصناعات؛ لذلك لزم القياس في إثبات صانع العالم بالعالم بما فيه من العجائب والأشياء التي لا يُحتمل كونها إلا بحكيم عليم ، ولا يجب به تعرف الكيفية له والمائية . ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And what they claimed concerning the origin and branch is inverted; because the Eternal and pre-eternity existed, and there was no means by which to infer, therefore it is not necessary to make it a branch of this; rather, it is the origin because this exists through it. Then everything that comes into existence through another, by way of reason, is external to its essence in the witnessed, like building, writing, and all types of actions and sayings that are other than those by whom they are brought about; it is not permissible to attach them to the essence and attribute, so the like of that by which the world exists. However, it is permissible in the witnessed to affirm what is not perceived or encompassed, like hearing, sight, spirit, intellect, desire, and the like, and what is perceived like dense bodies. So if they were eternal in origin, it would be necessary that every type be generated and arise from its essence: intellect from intellect, and likewise sight and hearing. And the difference between every essence and what is generated from it in that is known; so existence and origination are necessitated if it is different, and in establishing difference is the invalidation of the one in the description of pre-eternity being a world, or according to his attribute, and in that is the establishment of the origination of the world by Him who is unlike it. Moreover, writing indicates the writer, but does not indicate his modality or likeness, for it is possible that he be an angel, a human, or a jinn, so writing does not indicate the quiddity or modality of the writer, nor their like, and it indicates a writer of something. Similarly, the world with what it contains indicates an originator of something and does not indicate his modality or quiddity, and likewise building, weaving, carpentry, and crafts; therefore, analogy is necessitated in establishing the Maker of the world by the world with what it contains of wonders and things whose existence is not possible except from a wise, knowing one, and it is not necessary to know his modality and quiddity thereby. There is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage refutes the argument that the witnessed serves as an 'origin' (asl) for the unseen (far'). The author argues that the Eternal (al-Qadim) and pre-eternity existed before any means of inference, so the unseen is the origin, not the branch. Then he explains that things that come into existence through another (like building, writing) are external to the agent's essence, so we cannot attribute the agent's essence to the product. In the witnessed world, we affirm things that are not perceived (like hearing, sight) alongside dense bodies. If these were eternal in origin, then each type would have to generate from its own essence (e.g., intellect from intellect), but we see difference between the essence and what is generated. This establishes the world's origination and that the Creator is unlike the world. The analogy of writing: writing indicates a writer but not his nature or likeness; similarly, the world indicates a Maker but not His modality or quiddity. Therefore, we can infer the existence of a wise, knowing Creator without knowing His nature.

Key Terms
أصل
فرع
جوهر
صفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the created world can serve as an 'origin' (aṣl) to infer the nature of God as a 'branch' (farʿ).
Correction: The Eternal existed before any inference, so the unseen is the origin, not the branch. Products are external to the agent's essence, so we cannot derive God's attributes from the world.

Checkpoint
What does Māturīdī mean by 'what they claimed concerning the origin and branch is inverted'?
A) The origin is actually the branch
B) The Eternal existed before any inference, so it is the origin, not the branch
C) The seen world is the origin and God is the branch
D) Both the seen and unseen are equal

Key Takeaway
The Eternal is the origin, not a branch, and all created things are external to the essence of their Maker.

?

What would it look like to truly believe that they are merely external branches that exist through Allah alone? Write down one specific attachment you can actively reorient toward Allah today.
?
When you perform good deeds, do you ever feel that they are your own independent accomplishments? How does the lesson's principle that 'everything that comes into existence through another is external to that other's essence' humble you in your worship?
